<!-- 2026-06-22: cross-chat diagnosis brief "NEW-1" тАФ intermittent render crash on Schedule load
     ("Cannot read properties of undefined"), caught by the workspace ErrorBoundary (the non-chunk
     "Try again" variant), recovers on re-render. Highest B# across both files was B379, so minted
     **B380**. Per STANDING RULE #1 filed AND fixed + headless-verified (V105, regression net proven
     to FAIL with the guard off) the SAME session on branch `claude/relaxed-dijkstra-sokq4a` тАФ full
     [x] block lives in BACKLOG-DONE.md.
     ROOT CAUSE confirmed by reproduction, not guessed: the Schedule shell derives its breadcrumb's
     current project with `projects.find(p => p.id === activeId)` over the project list bridged from
     the embedded /sequence/ iframe (the brief's #1 candidate, Scheduler.jsx). The embedded app can
     transiently post a sparse/not-yet-resolved list (an `undefined`/null entry) during its own data
     load; one such entry makes `p.id` throw inside the Scheduler's render тЖТ the workspace boundary.
     A pure re-render recovers because the steady-state list is well-formed. (The brief's other
     candidates тАФ AppHeader/ProjectBreadcrumb p.id/p.name, useProfile/displayName тАФ were verified
     already null-safe; the deref that actually throws is the Scheduler's `.find`.)
     FIX (guard at the source, not optional-chaining everywhere): new pure `scheduler/lib/navState.js`
     тАФ `parseNavState` validates + `sanitizeProjects` coerces the inbound list to plain `{id,name}`
     objects (drops the throwing entries) and `deriveCurrentProject` never throws / never returns
     undefined; Scheduler.jsx routes the message + current-project derivation through them; one
     data-entry guard in the shared `ProjectBreadcrumb` (`.filter(Boolean)`) hardens its own `p.id`/
     `p.name` map for any controlled caller. NOT a chunk fix (not B221/B239) and NOT an ErrorBoundary
     auto-retry тАФ the race is removed so a genuine future crash still stays visible.

### B267 тАФ Auto-calibrate a sheet from its stated scale callout `[Doc Review / Markup]` (feature) #doc-review #markup  *(arrived as "NEW-3" 2026-06-20; renumbered **B267**; batch B265тАУB269)*
`[~]` Detect a stated-scale callout and **auto-set that sheet's calibration**, replacing the **"Sheet N not calibrated тАФ use Calibrate"** prompt (`DocReview.jsx`) when confidently found. **Per-sheet** (a set mixes scales; a sheet with no graphic scale stays uncalibrated, **never inherits a neighbour's**). **"NOT TO SCALE"/"AS NOTED"/unparseable тЖТ leave uncalibrated and say so explicitly** (*not present* тЙа *couldn't parse*).
- **тЬЕ Shipped this session тАФ embedded-text path (branch `claude/friendly-euler-hw8v1t`).** New **`parseSheetScale()`** (`overlayScale.js`) reads engineer's (1тА│=50тА▓), **architectural fractional** (1/4тА│=1тА▓-0тА│ тЖТ 4 ft/in), **ratio** (1:200), and explicit **NOT TO SCALE / AS NOTED** тАФ each with its own sane range; the civil `parseScaleNote` is left untouched (Site Planner overlay). `pdf.js` `extractPageText()` reads the page text; `DocReview.jsx` runs a **background per-sheet scan** on open тЖТ fills `calByPage` (gated on `detectSheet()` standard plot size) + a new `calInfo {src,label}` driving the sidebar (┬╖тЙИ auto / ┬╖тЬУ manual) and the badge ("scale from sheet тАж verify" / "NOT TO SCALE" / "calibrated"). Per-sheet, never overwrites a manual/loaded cal, persisted; opening a different file resets cals (a cross-document bleed bug found + fixed during verification). **7 unit tests + verified on the owner's real sets** (`ui-audit/verify-new3-autoscale.mjs`, **V67**): KG B1 **17/19** auto-calibrated (no-scale cover left alone), Jacintoport all **NOT TO SCALE**, 0 bleed. lint 0 ┬╖ 569 tests ┬╖ build green.
- **тП│ Remaining slice тАФ OCR fallback for scanned/raster sheets (owner: REQUIRED).** `extractPageText()` returns "" on a scanned page (the seam); the fallback (Tesseract.js in a Web Worker / server-side тЖТ rasterize тЖТ OCR тЖТ `parseSheetScale`) needs a **scanned sample** to build + verify (the owner's two sets are vector, so the shipped path covers them today). Kept `[~]` until OCR lands; shared OCR path with **B266**.
- **Design (as built):** extended `parseScaleNote`'s domain via a sibling `parseSheetScale` rather than loosening the civil 10тАУ1000 floor (architectural ft/in fall below it). A title-block "SCALE: NOT TO SCALE" wins outright; otherwise a real numeric plan scale beats a stray "NTS" detail note. Gated on `detectSheet()` + labeled "from sheet scale тАФ verify". Co-designs with **B268** (the geometry cross-check that catches a non-1:1 plot) / B181 / B182 / B183.

### B268 тАФ Independent scale cross-check against on-sheet geometry (verify the stated scale) `[Doc Review / Markup]` (feature) тАФ depends on B267 #doc-review #markup  *(arrived as "NEW-4" 2026-06-20; renumbered **B268**; batch B265тАУB269)*
`[ ]` After B267 sets a scale from text, **independently check** it by measuring a known on-sheet reference тАФ primarily the **graphic scale bar** (the printed ruler), which survives plotting/resizing where stated-scale text doesn't. Agree within tolerance тЖТ **"verified"**; disagree тЖТ **surface loudly, make the user choose тАФ never silently pick one** (silent wrong-calibration is crash-severity; it poisons every downstream takeoff). No scale bar тЖТ report **"no reference found"**, don't fail.
- **Decision recorded (owner's lean, matches the locked principle):** on disagreement **default to the scale bar (geometry) but flag it loudly**, one-click override to the stated scale тАФ *not* a silent choice. Matches **B182** ("geometry beats printed scale") + **B183** ("flag disagreement as a distinct state, never silently average/choose"). Flip to "always force a manual pick" if preferred.
- **Reuse:** **B183** already shipped the cross-check *primitives* for the Site Planner cascade; this is the **Markup-canvas application** to scale-bar-vs-stated-scale. **B181** captures the scale-bar facts. The owner's sets also carry **labeled dimensions** ("38тА▓-7 3/4тА│") тАФ a second independent reference.
> **Ready to build (largest of the three).** Needs **graphic-scale-bar detection/measurement** (locate the printed ruler on the raster + read its annotated length тАФ light CV), now testable on the owner's sets; depends on B267; ships *with* the loud-surface UI.

### B180 тАФ Project Files repository as a tagged-index with saved views `[Document Review / Files]` (feature) #doc-review #files  *(arrived as "NEW-1"; provisionally B176, renumbered **B180** тАФ #159 took B176тАУB179)*
`[~]` A project-level **file repository** opened from **Row 1 (the project-name area), NOT a fourth module tab.** Rationale (owner): tabs are *workspaces* (modes of working тАФ Site / Schedule / Markup); **Files is a shelf every workspace reaches into**, so it must be openable from inside any of them. "Folders" are **saved views over a tagged index, never a hand-maintained tree** тАФ "All surveys", "All title commitments", "this project's civil set" are all *queries* against file facts. Two document classes: **spatial** (can live on the map тАФ drawings, surveys, legal descriptions) vs **reference** (geotech, environmental, contracts тАФ pulled and read, never a map object); a **title commitment is BOTH** (a reference document, but Schedule A's legal description feeds the boundary polygon and Schedule B's exceptions feed easement objects). Drawer: files grouped by discipline; per-file state **Filed** (automatic) vs **On map** (calibrated once); a **drop zone** (auto-file by title block) and a **"needs filing"** holding area with one-click confirm for low-confidence / no-match.
- **тЬЕ Shipped this session (browser-first tranche, branch `claude/laughing-ritchie-k5narx`):**
  - **View-model engine** `src/shared/files/fileFacts.js` (pure, browser-free, **15 unit tests**): `classifyDocClass` (spatial / reference / **both** for title commitments + legal descriptions), `toFileFact`/`buildFileFacts` (normalizes the existing `listReviews` rows + defaults the NEW-2 placement facts), **`SAVED_VIEWS` + `runView`** (the saved-view query engine тАФ per-project in the drawer, **cross-project by dropping the project filter**, same query), `groupByDiscipline`, `fileState` (Filed vs On-map), `needsFiling` (holding area), and the **index-provider interface** `createIndexProvider`/`stubIndexProvider` тАФ the seam the auto-filing backend slots into with **no UI change** (`backendReady` flag keeps the UI honest about "auto-detected" vs "by hand").
  - **Drawer UI** `doc-review/components/ProjectFilesDrawer.jsx`, opened from **Row 1** (a ЁЯЧВ Files pill next to the project name in `DocReview.jsx`'s `centerContent`): saved-view chips, project picker + cross-project toggle, discipline groups, per-file **document-class tag** + **Filed/On-map** badge, a **drop zone** (files under the active project; auto-file-by-title-block flagged as backend), a **"needs filing"** holding area, and a **"Place on map"** action that runs the NEW-3 cascade (B182). lint 0 ┬╖ **290 tests** ┬╖ build green; the doc-review lazy chunk split still holds.
- **тП│ Follows the backend tranche (sanctioned by the owner's sequencing note тАФ stubbed behind `createIndexProvider`, not deferred work):** the **auto-filing index itself** (drop тЖТ read title block тЖТ match against the named projects + aliases тЖТ auto-route/auto-name; low-confidence тЖТ the holding area) тАФ this is the existing **auto-filing + lightweight-index** roadmap item and the **Google Drive auto-routing** item; **merge, do not duplicate.** Title-commitment тЖТ boundary polygon **reuses B25/B26's metes-and-bounds parser**; exceptions тЖТ easements **reuses B147's easements-as-first-class-objects** work. Privacy-first: **private by default** (rides the existing RLS).
> **Dedup:** generalizes **B14** (the `ProjectLibrary.jsx` explorer тАФ project тЖТ discipline тЖТ files), which stays as the in-workspace explorer; B180 is the **saved-views / tagged-index** surface reachable from Row 1 and adds document-class + Filed/On-map state. Distinct from **B67** (parcel-attached *pixel-space* markup). The "drop to open a PDF for viewing" roadmap item is the low-effort sibling; the title-block auto-filing is the backend feature тАФ two different timelines, kept separate.

### B181 тАФ Capture placement-readiness flags in file facts at filing time `[Document Review / Files]` (feature) #doc-review #files  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; provisionally B177, renumbered **B181** тАФ #159 took B176тАУB179)*
`[~]` At filing/index time, capture **more than discipline** so "Place on map" (B182) can pick its method **without reopening the file.** Per-drawing flags: **embedded real-world coordinates** present (+ source CRS); detectable **graphic scale bar** (yes/no + measured length + real length); **stated scale text** from the title block; **north arrow** present (+ orientation); visible **parcel/property boundary** present; **labeled dimensions** found (value + on-sheet endpoints). All cheap to capture during the title-block read pass.
- **тЬЕ Shipped this session:** the **fact schema + contract** `src/shared/placement/placementFacts.js` (pure): `emptyPlacementFacts()` (every sub-fact carries `present` so **"looked, found none" тЙа "never captured"** тАФ the silent-failure rule applied to placement), `PLACEMENT_FLAG_KEYS`, `mergePlacementFacts` (a partial/legacy capture is always a complete, safe object), and `longestDimension` (rung-3 baseline preference). Wired through `toFileFact` (every file fact carries a well-formed `placement`) and exercised by the cascade tests.
- **тП│ Follows the backend tranche (stubbed behind `createIndexProvider.capturePlacementFacts`):** the **actual capture** тАФ the title-block read pass that fills these in тАФ runs server-side as part of B180's auto-filing index. Until then the stub returns the empty shape and the cascade honestly lands on manual calibration (B183).
> **Dedup:** the capture piggybacks on B180's title-block read (one pass, not two). The scale-text parse reuses **B73's `parseScaleNote`/`detectSheet`** (`overlayScale.js`); embedded-coords/GeoPDF handling is B73's de-emphasized GeoPDF path.

### B182 тАФ "Place on map" auto-placement cascade `[Site Planner / Files]` (feature) #site-planner #files  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; provisionally B178, renumbered **B182** тАФ #159 took B176тАУB179)*
`[~]` On placing a filed drawing, walk methods **best тЖТ fallback** and **stop at the first that runs with confidence**; route every result through B183's verification before commit. Rungs: **(1) Embedded coordinates** тЖТ land exactly, no scaling (reproject to EPSG:2278); **(2) Fit to known boundary** тЖТ solve scale + rotation + translation in one affine/Helmert fit by matching the drawing's boundary to the held parcel/survey geometry тАФ **preferred over any stated scale** (a printed scale is a claim about original plot size and breaks under "fit to page"/copier resize; geometry is ground truth); **(3) Measure a graphic** тЖТ scale bar or labeled dimension, drawn length ├╖ annotated real value (resize-invariant), **prefer the longest baseline** (a 2 ft error over a 240 ft face is <1%; over a 24 ft bay it's 8%), use the north arrow for rotation then position to parcel; **(4) Manual calibration** тЖТ last resort (B183). Use the B181 flags to choose the rung; **never silently fall through a failed high rung without surfacing why.**
- **тЬЕ Shipped this session:** the **cascade orchestrator** `src/shared/placement/placeOnMap.js` (pure, **10 unit tests**): `RUNGS` (the 4 rungs in priority order, each with an `evaluate(facts, ctx)`), `choosePlacement(facts, ctx)` тЖТ `{ method, label, detail, skipped:[{method,reason}], confident, reason }` тАФ picks the best rung that runs **and lists every skipped higher rung with its reason** (the hard "no silent fall-through" rule), reads the B181 flags, prefers fit-to-boundary over stated scale, picks the **longest** dimension baseline, and carries the north-arrow rotation hint. Surfaced live in B180's drawer ("Place on map" тЖТ a plan panel naming the method + why higher ones were skipped).
- **тЬЕ Shipped this session тАФ rung-2 geometry:** the **fit-to-boundary solver** `src/shared/placement/fitToBoundary.js` (pure, **7 unit tests**): `fitToBoundary(source, target)` solves the one similarity (uniform scale + rotation + translation) that lands the drawing's boundary on the held parcel. Two paths тАФ **equal vertex counts** тЖТ exact correspondence search (every index rotation ├Ч both winding directions, closed-form Procrustes per candidate, lowest landing error wins; recovers sub-foot fits even when the rings start at a different corner and run the opposite way); **unequal counts** тЖТ an oriented-bounding-box fallback (match centroids, scale by тИЪarea ratio, best principal-axis rotation by nearest-vertex distance) for a sane starting placement. Returns `{ ok, transform:{scale,rotDeg,apply}, residual, residualFrac, confident, method, reason }`; `residualFrac` over тИЪarea flags a **distorted (non-rigid)** drawing a rigid fit can't honor (CONFIDENT_FRAC = 2%), per the silent-failure rule. Self-contained (its own Procrustes mirroring B73's `solveSimilarityLSQ`, no sharedтЖТworkspace import). This is the geometry the cascade invokes when `choosePlacement` returns the **fit-boundary** rung.
- **тП│ Still follows the backend tranche / EPSG spine:** **(1)** reprojection of embedded coords to EPSG:2278 (needs the coordinate spine wired, currently a stub in `src/shared/coordinates/`) and the **executor wiring** that takes the chosen rung's transform and actually repositions the overlay on the planner canvas; the **inputs** for rung 2 (the drawing's detected boundary + the held parcel geometry) come from B181's title-block read pass. **Rungs 3тАУ4 already exist** as the live B72/B73 overlay machinery (`overlayScale.js` scale/trace, `overlayAlign.js` similarity/affine fit) тАФ the cascade routes to them today. `choosePlacement`'s `ctx` (`canReproject`, `targetBoundary`) is the capability gate, so a rung only fires when its infra is present and otherwise reports *why* it's skipped.
> **Dedup:** this is the **decision layer over B72/B73**, not a second overlay engine. B72 = drop a PDF on the map + place by hand; B73 = scale calibration + trace + 2-point/N-point precise align (both shipped). B182 chooses *which* of those to apply automatically from the B181 facts. Severity: a confidently-wrong placement looks done and produces silently-wrong measurements тАФ **placement accuracy is HIGH severity** (the silent-failure rule), which is why every skipped rung is surfaced and every result is verified (B183).

### B183 тАФ Dimension-based calibration + auto-verification probe `[Site Planner / Document Review / Files]` (feature) #site-planner #doc-review #files  *(arrived as "NEW-4"; provisionally B179, renumbered **B183** тАФ #159 took B176тАУB179)*
`[~]` Resolves the open "precise-align / trace-a-known-dimension" question тАФ **answer: build it, and make it pull double duty.** **Calibration:** trace the two endpoints of a labeled dimension + type its value тЖТ derive scale (preferred over two arbitrary calibration points: it anchors to a value the drawing itself certifies); this is cascade rung 4. **Auto-verification:** after ANY placement method, find a labeled dimension, **measure it on the placed result, compare to the printed value, and surface a NUMBER** ("column grid measures 24.0 ft, label 24'-0" тАФ 0.1% off") тАФ not an eyeball confirmation. **Cross-check:** read two independent graphics (scale bar + a dimension, or two dimensions on different axes) and compare them **to each other**. Agreement тЖТ confident. Disagreement тЖТ **flag non-uniform scaling** (sheet stretched more in one axis, so no single uniform scale is valid) as a **distinct state тАФ do NOT silently average the two.**
- **тЬЕ Shipped this session:** the **calibration + verification primitives** `src/shared/placement/verifyPlacement.js` (pure, **8 unit tests**): `calibrateFromDimension` (rung-4 scale from a traced dimension), **`verifyDimension(measuredFt, labeledFt)`** тЖТ `{ pct, deltaFt, ok, severity:"ok|warn|bad", message }` (the probe that returns a number, with tight 1%/3% thresholds because takeoff rides on it), and **`crossCheckScales(samples)`** тЖТ `confident` (agree, reports the mean) / **`non-uniform`** (disagree тЖТ flags stretched-in-one-axis, **`meanScale:null` so it can never silently average**) / `insufficient`. The trace-a-known-dimension calibration itself already ships live in B73 (`overlayAlign.scaleOverlayAbout` + the canvas trace flow + Doc Review's calibrate-to-scale).
- **тП│ Follows the backend tranche:** the **auto-probe's data source** тАФ automatically *finding* a labeled dimension to measure on the placed result тАФ comes from B181's captured dimensions (read at filing time). Until then verification is available as the tested primitives (and can be driven by a hand-traced dimension); the auto-find runs once the title-block read pass lands. (A browser-only "trace a second dimension тЖТ cross-check" affordance on the live overlay is a small follow-on once the canvas flow is touched again.)
> **Dedup:** the calibration half is **B73's trace fallback** (don't rebuild it); B183 adds the **verification + cross-check** layer on top and is the function the B182 cascade calls after every placement. Reuses B73's `solveSimilarityLSQ` residual as the *rigid-fit* quality signal; `crossCheckScales` is the complementary *non-uniform-scale* signal (residual high **and** axes disagree тЖТ rubber-sheet needed, the B73 affine follow-on).

### B179 тАФ Backend per-account exact tax fetch `[server]` (feature) тАФ precision upgrade #infra  *(arrived as "NEW-4"; filed provisionally as B170, renumbered **B179** тАФ concurrent `main` took B167тАУB175, so this is the real next free ID after B175. This is the "A" path of the old B165 A/B decision тАФ built AFTER the browser "B" path, B176тАУB178, ships.)*
`[ ]` Per-county tax-office / appraisal-district account fetch that returns the **authoritative** taxing-unit list + rates matching the actual tax statement; upgrades the B177 panel from *screening* to *underwriting-grade*. **Server-side only** (lives in `/server`, the not-yet-built CAD/filing backend тАФ keep distinct from Supabase). Per-county field mapping (same registry pattern as parcel-source naming in `lib/counties.js`). Credentials/keys stay server-side, never in the browser bundle (KEY DECISIONS).
- **Why a backend:** HCAD's jurisdiction-rate page + per-account record pages return **HTTP 403 to automated clients** and there's no public CORS-open per-parcel rate REST endpoint (confirmed 2026-06-19) тАФ so authoritative rates can only be fetched server-side, where there's no CORS and the fetch can present a browser-like client.
- **Contract:** given county + account, return `{ units:[{name, rate}], total, asOf, source }`; the B177 panel swaps its screening rates for these and flips its header to "Verified ┬╖ <tax office>, <year>." On failure, the panel stays on screening (never blank).
- **Acknowledged multi-session:** depends on standing up `/server` first; may span its own session тАФ but implement, don't just file.
> **Supersedes the "A" half of B165.** Pluggable seam already exists (`TAX_RATE_SOURCES`/`resolveTaxRates`).

B179 (backend) is the authoritative upgrade.

### B171 тАФ Evaluate license-clean high-res imagery sources `[Site Planner]` (feature) #site-planner #gis  *(arrived as "NEW-3"; filed provisionally as B169, renumbered **B171** тАФ concurrent `main` took B167 + B168 for unrelated map items, so with the paired B169 (diagnostic) + B170 (retina fix) this is the real next free ID)*  тАФ GATED, do NOT action yet
`[ ]` **Gated on B169's finding + a confirmation step.** Only pick this up **if**, after B170's retina/HiDPI fix ships, the Esri World Imagery backdrop still looks **genuinely soft / stale** over the Houston metro on a real display. B169 showed the dominant blur causes were **(a) no HiDPI tiles and (b) the planner's fractional zoom тАФ NOT a low-res source** (Esri World Imagery is ~0.3 m/px native at z19), so this evaluation should **not** start until B170 is confirmed insufficient by eye. Add a **selectable** high-res basemap from a source that permits **tracing/measuring/derivative work** (Planyr users draw + measure site geometry over the aerial тАФ a hard licensing constraint).
- **Hard exclusion (licensing):** do **NOT** use **Google Maps satellite** (scraped `mt.google.com` tiles = TOS violation; even the paid Map Tiles API forbids tracing building outlines off satellite) or **Mapbox satellite** as the tracing backdrop (commercial derivative tracing needs a paid Commercial Satellite license). Both are ruled out for Planyr's core use case regardless of sharpness.
- **Candidate sources, in order:** (1) **Texas Imagery Service** (formerly TNRIS) state orthoimagery; (2) **Houston-metro county appraisal-district orthos** (public record, often 6-inch, very current); (3) **NAIP** (federal, public domain) as a national fallback. All are traceable + license-clean.
- **Verify each endpoint against a known Katy parcel** for coverage, resolution, and recency **before** wiring it in тАФ don't assume availability (county/state GIS hosts move and stop often; rely on the existing probe + honest error surfacing).
- **Premium AEC imagery** (Nearmap / Vexcel / Maxar, properly licensed) is a **future paid-tier** upgrade, **not in scope** here.
- Treat **imagery age/source as surfaceable metadata** (consistent with the "always surface data age" principle for the GIS layers).
> **Dedup:** distinct from **B162** (street-label zoom gating) and **B65** (white-flash on zoom/pan); this is about the *imagery source/resolution itself*. Builds on the swappable-basemap registry that already exists (`BASEMAPS` in `MapFinder.jsx` тАФ Esri + USGS today), so adding a source is a registry row + a picker entry, not bespoke plumbing.

### B147 тАФ Site Analysis tool: multi-parcel constraint & context screen `[Site Planner / Site Analysis]` (feature) #site-planner #gis  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted **B147** тАФ highest existing ID was B146, so this is the real next free ID. "NEW-2" is only a scratch label from the arriving chat тАФ B120/B134/B145 also "arrived as NEW-2".)*
`[ ]` A dedicated **Site Analysis** tool (working name тАФ module naming not finalized) that runs environmental, regulatory, and infrastructure screening against the **combined footprint of the selected parcels** and presents findings **grouped by category**, presence-first. This is the **single home** for the checks currently buried in the parcel-info popup and for the **Tier 1 "site-killer" roadmap** in CLAUDE.md тАФ build it as ONE surface; do **NOT** spin up a parallel one (see the reconciliation flags below).
- **Input geometry:** the **dissolved union of the active parcels** (the "site") тАФ never a centroid, click point, or single parcel. Reuse **B100**'s `activeParcelsOf` selector so the screened footprint matches the same parcels yield/coverage/detention already use; exclude inactive parcels. **DECIDED 2026-06-17 (Michael): screen the ACTIVE-only union** (not all selected parcels) тАФ confirmed consistent with the yield/coverage/detention math, so no remaining ambiguity here.
- **Finding categories** (v1 = presence + the single most decision-relevant attribute; detail-on-expand):
  - **Floodplain** тАФ FEMA NFHL (National Flood Hazard Layer = FEMA's digital flood maps). Zone designation(s) intersecting the site + rough extent. *(Maps to the Tier 1 "finished-floor vs. base-flood" item тАФ reconcile, don't duplicate; reuses the FEMA overlay already wired in B129/B133.)*
  - **Wetlands** тАФ USFWS NWI (National Wetlands Inventory = the federal desktop wetlands map). Presence + classification. **Hard caveat: screening only тАФ NOT a jurisdictional delineation;** a consultant delineation + USACE verification is required for any real determination. *(Reuses the NWI overlay from B133/B135.)*
  - **Pipelines** тАФ PHMSA NPMS (PHMSA = the federal pipeline-safety agency; NPMS = its National Pipeline Mapping System) + RRC. **Caveat: public NPMS is deliberately low-resolution for security** тАФ a flag to trigger 811/one-call + operator outreach, never a precise alignment.
  - **Oil & gas features** тАФ RRC (Railroad Commission of Texas тАФ the state oil/gas regulator, despite the name). Well bores (active / plugged / abandoned) + surface locations. **Caveat: historic well locations can be inaccurate or unmapped;** an RRC records search (possibly a survey) is the real check. High relevance for Houston-area sites (orphaned wells).
  - **Environmental contamination** тАФ TCEQ LPST (Texas Commission on Environmental Quality, Leaking Petroleum Storage Tank database) + EPA sites. *(Maps to the Tier 1 "environmental screen (TCEQ LPST / EPA)" item тАФ reconcile, don't duplicate.)*
  - **Jurisdiction** тАФ city limits / ETJ / county / road authority. **This is B93 (shipped) + B94 (open) re-homed as a SECTION here, not a standalone Identify-panel button or popup field** тАФ the discoverability fix (see below).
  - **Zoning / entitlement** тАФ jurisdiction-dependent; pulled from the jurisdiction context. **Note: City of Houston has NO zoning тАФ don't build as if every jurisdiction has it;** ETJ-area and other cities vary. *(Maps to the Tier 1 "entitlement/zoning" item; the per-jurisdiction rules are B95's "development-consequence summary" тАФ reconcile.)*
- **Presentation:** findings grouped by category, **presence-first** тАФ a clear **present / not-present / unknown** state per category, detail on expand. **Each finding carries its own data source + data-age stamp + a category-specific screening caveat тАФ NOT one blanket disclaimer.**
- **тШЕ Silent-error principle (HIGH severity):** **"Unknown / source unavailable" is a DISTINCT state from "not present."** A failed or timed-out source must **never** render as "no constraint." Reuses the existing honest per-layer status (B96/B129) тАФ surface the failure, don't swallow it.
- **Architecture reuse (no parallel system, no new credentials):** runs on the **existing generic ArcGIS-REST connector + source registry** (`lib/jurisdiction.js` / `lib/vectorLayers.js`) + the **GIS stale-while-revalidate cache (B96)** + honest per-layer status. Each new source (NFHL, NWI, NPMS, RRC, TCEQ/EPA) is **a registry row, not bespoke code.** Browser-only where the sources are public REST services.
> **Dedup / reconciliation тАФ these are NOT new items; fold this work into / build it on top of them (each aware of the other, never a forked parallel surface):**
> - **B93 (jurisdiction identify тАФ DONE, shipped + verified live) + B94 (road authority тАФ open):** **re-home the jurisdiction/road-authority identify as a SECTION inside Site Analysis**, not the standalone "тЪЦя╕О Jurisdiction & road authority" Identify-panel button it ships as today (and never a popup field). This is the **discoverability fix** the arriving note asks for тАФ same engine, surfaced inside the analysis tool.
> - **CLAUDE.md Tier 1 "site-killer" roadmap** (storm outfall, sanitary sewer, fire flow, finished-floor-vs-base-flood, environmental screen, entitlement/zoning): these are **Site Analysis sections, not a parallel surface** тАФ reconcile so they render in THIS tool. (Storm outfall / sanitary sewer / fire flow are infrastructure sections to add alongside the v1 categories above.)
> - **B95 (jurisdiction тЖТ development-consequence summary тАФ DEFERRED):** its per-jurisdiction rules (who regulates platting, whether zoning applies, who reviews drainage/detention + fire flow, who permits access) feed the **Zoning/entitlement + Jurisdiction sections** here тАФ the consequence layer surfaces *in* Site Analysis when it's picked up.
> - **B96 (GIS SWR cache тАФ open):** the cache + honest-status mechanism this tool rides on; B96 stays the foundation (sequence accordingly).
> - **B98 (parcel-popup declutter тАФ DONE) + B100 (active/inactive parcels тАФ DONE):** **heavy analysis moves OUT of the parcel-info popup into Site Analysis; the popup keeps only lightweight parcel identity (owner/name, ID, area).** Input footprint = B100's active-parcel union (see Input geometry above).
> - **FEMA/NWI overlay layers (B129/B133/B135):** the Floodplain + Wetlands findings reuse those already-wired overlays as their data source тАФ read them, don't re-plumb them.
> **тШЕ v1 SHIPPED 2026-06-19 (branch `claude/trusting-allen-xatlua`) тАФ the tool now exists as ONE surface; remaining categories are registry rows.** Built the whole Site Analysis surface on the existing infra (no parallel system, no new credentials): a new registry-driven connector `lib/siteAnalysis.js` rides the same SWR cache (B96) + the verified jurisdiction engine (B93/B94, `jurisdiction.js`) + EPSG:4326 boundary as the parcel identify, and a new `components/SiteAnalysis.jsx` panel opened from a new **"тЪР Analysis"** left-rail tab. It screens the **dissolved footprint of the ACTIVE parcels** (B100's `active !== false`, converted to lon/lat rings via `feetToLatLng`) as a single multipolygon intersect, and presents findings **presence-first, grouped by category**, each with its own source + data-age + a category-specific caveat (no blanket disclaimer).
> **тШЕ The silent-error principle is enforced in code + unit-tested (HIGH severity):** a finding is `present` / `absent` / `unknown` / `info` / `pending`, and `classifyStatus` only reports a confident **"None found"** for a `verified` source returning empty тАФ an unverified or errored source reads **UNKNOWN, never a fabricated all-clear**. Pending categories read **"source not connected"** (distinct from "none").
> **Categories wired in v1:** **Floodplain** (FEMA NFHL layer 28, `verified`), **Jurisdiction** (city/ETJ/county) + **Road authority** + **Zoning/entitlement** (derived: HoustonтЖТno zoning, other cityтЖТzoning likely, unincorporatedтЖТno county zoning) тАФ all reusing `jurisdiction.js`. **Wetlands** (NWI staging split layers 1,2), **Oil & gas wells** + **Pipelines** (TxRRC via the Harris County GIS host) are wired but `verified:false` (their /query reliability is unconfirmed, so empty тЖТ honest unknown). **Environmental contamination** (TCEQ LPST / EPA) is a `pending` registry row (no confirmed CORS-clean endpoint yet) тЖТ reads "source not connected." Adding/verifying any source later = flipping a registry row, not new code.
> **Tests + verification:** new `test/siteAnalysis.test.js` (28 cases: geometry/query building, summarizers, the present/absent/unknown guard, multi-sublayer query, cache ride, jurisdiction-throw resilience, full orchestration order). lint **0 errors** ┬╖ **285 tests** ┬╖ build green ┬╖ `SitePlannerApp` lazy chunk intact. **Self-verified headless on the built app** (`gis-verify/site-analysis-verify.{mjs,png}`): seeded a georeferenced Katy parcel тЖТ Analysis tab тЖТ **Floodplain = PRESENT "Zone AE, X"** (live FEMA), **Jurisdiction = Fort Bend / Katy**, **Road = State (TxDOT)┬╖City**, **Zoning = "Within Katy тАФ city zoning applies"** (live), and the sandbox-blocked Wetlands/Pipelines/Wells correctly read **UNKNOWN ("Failed to execute query")**, Environmental **"Not connected"** тАФ the honest-state path confirmed.
> **ЁЯФ▓ Remaining (kept open тАФ the additional-categories + polish tranche):** (1) **verify + flip** Wetlands / Pipelines / Oil&gas to confident `absent`-capable once their /query + correct sublayers are browser-confirmed (today they degrade to unknown, which is safe but conservative); (2) wire a real **TCEQ LPST / EPA** contamination source (the pending registry row); (3) add the **Tier-1 infrastructure sections** (storm outfall, sanitary sewer, fire flow) as registry rows in this same tool; (4) **re-home the in-Identify "тЪЦя╕О Jurisdiction & road authority" button** fully into Site Analysis (today it still also lives on the point-identify result тАФ kept to avoid regressing that flow); (5) signed-in/live planyr.io click-through (the sandbox proved the path with live FEMA + TxDOT, but a real-display pass is worth logging).

### B115 тАФ Revisit keyboard shortcuts: memorability + let the owner remap them `[Site Planner / UI]` (task) тАФ owner-gated #site-planner #ui
`[ ]` Owner note (2026-06-16): the planner's single-key shortcuts are hard to remember and Michael may want to change them тАФ **park this for a deliberate pass with him; do NOT unilaterally rename keys.** Decide together: (a) whether the current assignments stay, (b) whether to make them **user-remappable** (a small settings screen + persisted overrides) vs. just keep a fixed, better-surfaced set, and (c) whether any are non-obvious / collide with muscle memory (e.g. **S** could read as "save"). Current bindings, for reference when picked up: **V** Select ┬╖ **H** Pan (+ hold **Space** = temp pan) ┬╖ **S** toggle Snap (new, B114) ┬╖ **Q** Callout ┬╖ **T** Text ┬╖ **L** Line ┬╖ **R** Rect ┬╖ **E** Ellipse ┬╖ **тЗзP** Polygon ┬╖ **тЗзN** Polyline ┬╖ **Ctrl/тМШ Z / тЗзZ / Y** undo/redo ┬╖ **Ctrl/тМШ C / X / V / D** copy/cut/paste/duplicate ┬╖ **Delete/тМл** delete ┬╖ **Esc** cancel ┬╖ **?** shortcuts panel; gestures **тЗз-drag** bond-to-neighbour, **Alt-drag** bypass-snap (B114). All are already listed in-app under the **?** panel. No code change yet тАФ awaiting the owner's preferences.

### B13 тАФ Refine B11 county resolution: precise boundaries + per-area jurisdiction `[Site Planner / map]` (feature) #site-planner #gis
`[ ]` Follow-up to **B11** (shipped in PR #13) тАФ two interim simplifications captured here so they aren't forgotten. Neither is urgent; both are screening-only conveniences today and degrade gracefully.
- **Coarse bbox pre-filter тЖТ real point-in-county.** B11 routes a parcel click to a CAD service using *approximate* per-county bounding boxes (a coarse screen; the CAD that actually returns a lot is the source of truth, with a fall-back to querying all counties). Fine for the 3 configured counties (Harris / Fort Bend / Chambers), but as more counties are added, switch to true point-in-county boundary polygons so the pre-filter stays accurate and cheap. **(STILL OPEN.)**
- **Layers panel jurisdiction is hardcoded to Harris/Houston.** ~~With no county pre-picked, the map's Layers panel defaults to the Harris/Houston jurisdictionтАж~~ **DONE** тАФ the map Layers panel jurisdiction now follows the map's current area.
> Progress 2026-06-15 (this PR): **point 2 done** тАФ the map's Layers panel jurisdiction is no longer hardcoded to Harris; `MapFinder` resolves `viewCounty` from the view centre via `candidateCountiesForPoint` on every `moveend`, so the correct utility overlays are offered outside Houston (falls back to Harris when the centre is outside all configured counties; per-site jurisdiction still follows the opened site's county). **Point 1** (true point-in-polygon county boundaries vs. the bbox pre-filter) remains open тАФ the bbox screen is still adequate for the 3 configured counties, so this is deferred until more counties are added.
>
> **What this is (plain English, 2026-06-15) тАФ the "county resolution" theme.** B13-pt1 + **B36(a)** + **B36(d)** are really one piece of work: *how the app decides which county's appraisal-district (CAD) service to query when you click the map.* Today it screens by approximate per-county **bounding boxes** тАФ fine for interior clicks in the 3 configured counties (Harris / Fort Bend / Chambers). The gaps, all near a county border or when a 4th+ county is added: **B13-pt1** the bboxes overlap/approximate тЖТ replace with true county **boundary polygons** (point-in-polygon); **B36(a)** the statewide TxGIO fallback can mislabel a Harris/FB lot's `county` when the primary CAD returns nothing; **B36(d)** a click on a county line should query both CADs and merge (only the first hit is used today). **Needs a county-boundary GIS dataset** to load + test points against тАФ a data-source decision, so it's **feature-scale, not a quick fix**, and **low urgency** (interior clicks in the current 3 counties are fine). When picked up: choose/confirm the boundary source first, then point-in-polygon resolution + straddle merge fall out of it.
>
> **Progress 2026-06-15 (branch `claude/festive-davinci-0oco2n`): the point-in-county primitive now exists.** B72 landed the verified TxDOT county-boundary layer, and `lib/jurisdiction.js` `countyAtPoint(lng,lat)` resolves the true county (cached) and maps it to a configured CAD key тАФ exactly the dataset/primitive this item was waiting on. **Pt 1's routing SWAP is deliberately NOT done:** the existing parallel "query candidate CADs, answerer wins" identify is faster + more resilient than a blocking point-in-county lookup before every click, so replacing the bbox pre-filter would regress, not improve. The primitive is instead used additively for the **B36(a)** label correction (see B36's note). The data gap pt 1 cited is closed; the bbox pre-filter stays by choice.

### B128 тАФ Import reported 3 sites but the account total rose by 2 тАФ confirm all imports land `[Persistence]` (bug) тАФ low, needs repro #persistence
`[ ]` From the V15 cohort run (T4, signed-in): the `importLegacyIntoCloud` banner said "**3** sites brought into your account" but the account count went **15тЖТ17** (not 18). Non-destructive (local copies kept) so **no loss**, but one import may not have landed. Investigate: a failed push counted optimistically, an id collision/dedupe, or just a stale display count. Needs a clean repro on throwaway sites тАФ check `importLegacyIntoCloud`'s `copied/skipped/failed` against the actual account-list count, and confirm all three rows are queryable in `public.sites`.

### B131 тАФ Clip a generated parking field to the parcel boundary `[Site Planner]` (feature) тАФ large lift #site-planner  *(split out of B130; minted B131 тАФ next after B130)*
`[ ]` When a parking field (and its double-loaded module fill) extends past the parcel / usable-area boundary, clip the generated stalls + aisles to that boundary instead of drawing and counting pavement outside it тАФ so stall yield reflects only what actually fits on the site. Called out as **out of scope** in B130 (that layout engine fills a drawn rectangle; this trims the fill to an arbitrary boundary). Large lift: needs rectangle-vs-polygon clipping of the stall bands, a yield recount on the clipped set, partial-stall handling at the cut, and the curb rule re-applied to the clipped perimeter. Builds on the existing parking generator (`carStalls` / `lib/parking.js`) + the parcel / usable-area polygon.

### B134 тАФ Edits silently lost on reload; app loads a stale earlier state `[Persistence]` (bug) тАФ DATA-LOSS, critical #persistence  *(arrived as "NEW-2"; minted B133, renumbered B134 amid concurrent merges; its sibling SCHIEL-recovery item ultimately landed at B136)*
`[ ]` **Repro:** (1) open planyr.io, sign in; (2) load/build a Site Planner plan and make edits (e.g. add buildings until the plan is materially larger); (3) hard-reload with `Ctrl+Shift+R`. **Observed:** the plan reverts to an earlier saved state, recent edits gone, no error shown. **Expected:** after ANY reload (normal F5 or hard `Ctrl+Shift+R`), the most recent saved state loads intact тАФ newer work is never silently replaced by an older state.
- Part of: **B648** (Persistence & Sync epic).
> **Diagnostic note:** `Ctrl+Shift+R` bypasses the HTTP cache but does NOT clear localStorage, IndexedDB, sessionStorage, or cookies. Work vanishing on a hard reload therefore means it was never durably saved (or the loader prefers a stale source) тАФ the reload did not delete it. Isolate the layer first by testing F5 vs `Ctrl+Shift+R` vs a fresh tab vs tab-close; that tells you whether the gap is in-memory-only, local storage, service-worker cache (the background script that can cache the app), or cloud.
> **Candidate causes, rough priority** (confirm with the signed-in headless browser; capture network + console):
> 1. ~~**Supabase "Cloud off"**~~ тАФ **RULED OUT 2026-06-17 (this session):** the live planyr.io shell bundle has the Supabase URL `lyeqzkuiwngunutlkkmi.supabase.co` baked in, so cloud IS configured/on. (`VITE_SUPABASE_URL` / `VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY` are baked in at BUILD time, not runtime; a build missing them ships a cloud-off client that silently falls back to device-only storage тАФ "has bitten twice" тАФ but that is NOT the case on the current deploy.)
> 2. **Browser-storage quota** тАФ if cloud is off and the app falls back to localStorage, a growing plan can cross the browser's ~5 MB local-storage cap and writes start throwing `QuotaExceededError`, silently dropping saves. Fits the symptom exactly (smaller plan saved, larger one did not). If so, move plan state to IndexedDB (far larger limit) and/or fix cloud.
> 3. **Save not firing / debounce race** тАФ if autosave is debounced (waits for a pause in editing before writing), reloading before the timer fires loses the last edits. Flush on `visibilitychange`/`beforeunload` and on explicit navigation.
> 4. **Save firing but erroring silently** тАФ the Supabase write returns 401/403 (expired auth token, or a row-level-security rule blocking the write), 409 (conflict), or a swallowed network error. Surface and log every save failure.
> 5. **Wrong load precedence / record mismatch** тАФ newer work saved locally but on boot the loader fetches the cloud copy and the stale cloud version clobbers it (or vice versa); or edits save under a different plan id/version/key than the loader reads. Make load deterministic: newest-wins by timestamp, single source of truth.
> Likely lives in the shared cloud save/load layer, so fix it workspace-agnostically even though it surfaced in Site Planner.
> **Dedup / cross-refs тАФ filed net-new: same SYMPTOM class as B124, but a fresh live recurrence that raises two UNINVESTIGATED root causes.** Same "data loss on reload" symptom as **B124** (Schiel/JFK), whose root cause (the `pullCloud` thin-merge + the two-store split) was found and fixed in **B126/B127**, with the loud-failure half in **B125** тАФ and **тШЕ corrected 2026-06-17 (this session): all of B124/B125/B126/B127 are MERGED (PRs #81/#83/#85/#89) AND DEPLOYED to live planyr.io** (the live `SitePlannerApp` chunk carries the B126 version-history key `planarfit:sites:history:v1` + the "Version history" dialog + the B125 "Retry now" banner; the shell has the Supabase URL baked in тЖТ **cloud is ON**). So the recurrence is **NOT unmerged code and NOT cloud-off тАФ both ruled out**, which eliminates candidate #1 and #2's cloud-off premise. Refocus on the causes the shipped fixes do NOT cover: **#3** (the 10-building state never durably persisted тАФ a debounced cloud push that didn't fire before the reload, so the loader fell back to the older 6-building cloud copy; B126's union-merge only recovers work that reached a store, not work that never persisted тАФ the closest fit), **#4** (a silent save error тАФ expired auth token / RLS 401тАУ403 / 409), or **#5** (load precedence). Also overlaps the historical **B18** (last-debounce-window edits flush local-only) and **B54** (`pullCloud` overwrites the cache with `{}` on a fetch error). If the investigation pins the live cause to one of those, note it both here and there rather than re-fixing. The visible-status guardrail is **B125** (it would have surfaced this immediately); the SCHIEL recovery action is **B136**.
> **Progress 2026-06-17 (this session, branch `claude/nice-ptolemy-9j0u7g`): the load-precedence half (#5) is FIXED in code.** Root cause pinned in the boot sequence: `SitePlannerApp` renders the planner `key={activeSiteId}` and the planner snapshots its plan from storage **once at mount**; the first synchronous render runs BEFORE auth resolves (`activeUser` still null тЖТ reads the legacy/local store), so a signed-in user can paint a stale copy тАФ and the authoritative copy that `applyUser`'s `pullCloud` merges in is a **same-tab `localStorage` write (fires no `storage` event)**, so the already-mounted planner never refreshes. Exactly the owner's "showed 6 buildings, then came back to 10 on its own." Fix: a `loadEpoch` bumped after the boot/sign-in pull and folded into the planner's `key`, forcing a one-time remount so the resumed plan re-reads the freshly-merged store. **Display/load-timing only тАФ the save/merge/version-history logic is untouched, so it cannot worsen data safety** (worst case is a sub-second remount). lint 0 errors ┬╖ 191 tests ┬╖ build green ┬╖ lazy split intact. **Still OPEN:** causes **#3 (never-persisted / debounce-flush gap)** and **#4 (silent save error)** тАФ the true-loss cases where work never reached any store тАФ need the visible/honest save-status + flush work tracked in **B125/NEW-3**. **Verification gap:** the sandbox browser can't sign in, so the signed-in boot path needs a signed-in click-through to confirm end-to-end; the change is gated to the signed-in resume branch, so logged-out behavior is unchanged. **The signed-in end-to-end browser confirmation is logged as VERIFICATION V28** тАФ the "limit" this session couldn't self-run (sandbox can't sign in); a signed-in coworker runs it down.
> **Amendment 2026-07-11 (candidate #2, browser-storage quota тАФ diagnostics, corrected).** An adversarial-review brief flagged the quota path again; auditing it against current code, the raw premise is now mostly **stale**, but the residual is worth recording. Confirmed live: `gisCache` still budgets itself **3 MB** of the ~5 MB origin quota (`maxTotalBytes`, `lib/gisCache.js`), and the per-user cloud cache + the version-history ring add pressure. HOWEVER the brief's core claim тАФ that the `writeSites` quota fallback "fails to slim the two raster fields that actually get large" тАФ is **false against HEAD**: B473/B474 made both the proactive path (`dropIdbBackedSrc`) and the over-quota retry (`stripDataUrls`) shed **all three** raster homes (`underlay` / `sheetOverlays` / `parcelDrawings`), and B474 moved those rasters onto IndexedDB (localStorage sits ~700 KB even with big images), so the specific "large overlay defeats the retry тЖТ save silently drops" failure can no longer occur. What's NOT yet built (filed, not a data-loss bug): `writeSites` never asks `gisCache` to yield FIRST (no `gisCache.trim(bytes)` API; screening cache is regenerable, user data is not) тАФ a pre-emptive optimization, tracked as the gisCache-eviction bullet under the quota theme, not here. So candidate #2 stays a *possible* contributor only via the gis-cache-starves-headroom angle (overlaps **B483**), not via the raster-strip gap the brief described.
> **Amendment 2026-06-30 тАФ a DISTINCT sixth root cause in this same symptom family was found + fixed: B594/B595.** An owner report ("I drew a polyline and it disappeared") triggered a fresh adversarial audit that pinned a cause NOT in the #1тАУ#5 list: drawn-element ids came from a per-tab counter that `ensureIdAbove` re-seeded only from parcels+els, so a freshly drawn markup could reuse a **tombstoned** id (after a reopen) or **collide** across two tabs тАФ and `mergeSiteContent`'s tombstone filter then stripped the live item mid-session (then persisted the loss). Fixed by salting `uid()` (new `src/shared/ids.js`) + seeding `ensureIdAbove` from all collections+tombstones (**B594**), and the count-only read-back that let it pass silently was made membership-anchored (**B595**). This does not close #3/#4 (still the open debounce-flush / silent-error cases) but removes the most-likely real-world trigger of "work vanished on its own." Live two-tab signed-in repro = V185.

### B20 тАФ `setProjectStatus` rewrites every plan in the group via `cloudUpsert` (strips inline underlay, heavy, clobber risk) `[Document Review]` (bug) тАФ correctness, medium #doc-review #persistence
`[ ]` Flipping a project's status from the library round-trips each site row's whole `data` through `cloudUpsert`, which `slimForCloud`-strips any still-inline `data:` underlay and bumps `updated_at` on every plan (can clobber a concurrent edit). Cloud copies are usually already slimmed so true loss is unlikely, but a status dropdown shouldn't rewrite full site blobs. Fix: a minimal status-only write (jsonb patch/RPC) or guard the underlay before re-upsert.
> Deferred 2026-06-15 (future reference): the clean "status-only write" needs a Postgres RPC / `jsonb_set` тАФ a backend/migration change, same class as B47a's `ESCAPE`, so not done client-side. Low-risk in practice today: cloud `data` is already underlay-slimmed (the strip is usually a no-op), and the serialтЖТparallel + partial-failure reporting landed in B56c. Revisit when the `/server` backend exists.

### B38 тАФ SQL/RLS & data-integrity audit (mostly clean) `[Document Review / DB]` (bug) тАФ minor #doc-review #persistence
`[ ]` A dedicated schema/RLS pass **verified the new code is sound**: both `doc_reviews` and the `sites`/storage policies are owner-scoped (all 4 verbs, `to authenticated`, no `public`/anon/admin), the bucket is private, every client storage path hardcodes uid as the leading segment (so `(storage.foldername(name))[1]` RLS can't be bypassed), both migrations are idempotent, the `(user_id,id)` PK matches every `onConflict`, and the `doc_date` empty-stringтЖТ`null` boundary holds. Remaining minors: (a) **storage orphaning** тАФ `uploadSource` uses `upsert:true` on a path derived from current project/discipline, so re-filing + re-uploading a source leaves the old object behind (key in `sources[]` is overwritten, so cleanup can't find it); fix by keying objects on the immutable `srcId` only, or deleting the prior key first. (b) `upsertReview`'s pre-migration fallback never **back-fills** the index columns for rows saved before the migration (a later normal edit self-heals that row; values always live in `data` jsonb meanwhile); the fallback regex (`/column|.../`) is also broad. (c) `setProjectStatus` writes rows back through `cloudUpsert` without `createSiteModel` normalization (lossless passthrough, but a status edit could also heal a legacy row if normalized). (`deleteReview` user-scoping тАФ fixed in the audit PR alongside B37a.)
> Deferred 2026-06-15 (future reference): (a) the clean fix changes the Storage object-key scheme (or deletes the prior key on re-file) тАФ migration/orphan implications, wants a live repro before shipping; an orphaned object only wastes quota, nothing breaks. (b)/(c) are trivial/self-healing (a later normal edit backfills the index columns / normalizes the row). Low urgency тАФ pick up when storage cleanup is worth a dedicated pass.

### B63 тАФ Parallel-session merge safety: branch тЖТ PR тЖТ green-build gate `[repo / workflow]` (task) #infra #testing
`[ ]` Guardrail so two concurrent Claude Code sessions can't silently break `main`. git already catches *same-line* collisions (it refuses тАФ the safe, loud case); the real risk is two sessions editing *different but interdependent* files тЖТ clean merge, broken app, which only re-building the **combined** result catches. **Active practice (already followed; make it explicit in CLAUDE.md):** each session works on its own branch, never commits to `main`; finishes via a PR; before merge, restacks on the latest `main` and re-runs the build, merging only if green; one PR per backlog item where practical. The *enforced* GitHub branch-protection half is parked under ЁЯХУ Later (needs a paid plan on this private repo + a one-time owner toggle).

### B95 тАФ Jurisdiction тЖТ development-consequence summary `[Site Planner / GIS]` (task, downstream тАФ DEFERRED) #site-planner #gis
`[ ]` Optional downstream layer: translate the raw boundary facts from **B93 / B94** into the questions that drive a deal тАФ who regulates platting/subdivision (city directly / city-via-ETJ / county), whether zoning applies (Houston has none; most others do), who reviews drainage/detention and fire flow, which property-tax jurisdictions apply, and who issues the access permit (from B94).
- Plugs into the existing **verdict-engine** concept (the `developableArea()` synthesis stub); stays a **screening aid, not legal advice.**
- **Defer until B93 / B94 are solid.** Rules are per-jurisdiction and accrue over time тАФ start with Houston plus the 2тАУ3 most common cities and expand as hit.

### B824 тАФ One home for drainage: merge the Analysis "Floodplain mitigation & buildability" card into Yield тЖТ Stormwater; Analysis keeps a one-line screening verdict `[Site Planner / yield ┬╖ analysis]` (feature) #site-planner #yield #ui #export  *(owner 2026-07-13 тАФ "everything related to detention and drainage in one spotтАж I'm assuming the yield tool"; minted **B824**)*
`[ ]` Today the same engine renders in two tabs тАФ Yield's stormwater readout (`SitePlanner.jsx:14555+`) and Site Analysis's sibling card (`components/FloodMitigationCard.jsx:35`, mounted at `SitePlanner.jsx:9860` under `<SiteAnalysis/>`; B712) тАФ a split-brain: an input changed in Yield silently changes a card the user isn't looking at. Sequence **before or with B823** (the copy pass happens once, here).
- Verify: live (PDF/export parity class + the B712/V243 interplay)
- Origin: filed 2026-07-14 from chat ("NEW-5")
- **Design:** Yield тЖТ Stormwater becomes the single drainage surface, organized as collapsed verdict groups тАФ Detention ┬╖ Floodplain mitigation ┬╖ Buildability / FFE тАФ each one verdict line, expanding to the detail that currently lives on the Analysis card (per-class ledger, providers, derivation notes, pathway/LOMR-F flags, ┬з404-wetlands screen); all inputs stay here. тЪа Honest scoping vs the chat draft: "B803-style collapsed groups" is NEW UI тАФ B803 shipped one-line-per-concept + тУШ (native title) + a single Advanced fold; `groupHead` (`SitePlanner.jsx:14453`) is a static header, not a collapse control. The merged section renders COLLAPSED by default (verdict lines only) тАФ the B823 one-line cap applies to everything that moves.

### B691 тАФ Fort Bend 1-ft contours layer dead: browser CORS-blocks `arcgisweb.fortbendcountytx.gov` тАФ route it through the server-side GIS proxy (├Ч2) `[Site Planner / GIS]` (bug) #site-planner #gis  *(surfaced 2026-07-07 in the Cowork element-sync live run тАФ console showed the layer's `тАж/FLOODZONE/Contours_1Foot/MapServer?f=json` probe failing CORS on planyr.io)*

Same class as other locked-down county endpoints: route the request through the existing same-origin server-side GIS proxy pattern (a Pages Function fetches server-side, where CORS doesn't apply, and relays JSON to the app) instead of calling the county host directly from the page. The noise is real UX harm even where the layer self-heals via the proxy retry тАФ silence the DIRECT probe, don't just document around it. (Arrived as chat item "NEW-2"; DEDUPE-FIRST тАФ it is the probe half of this item's existing scope, so no new number.)

The layer row's тУШ notes "health via proxy (host sends no CORS headers)". Only one tab can edit at a time; the others are read-onlyтАж" with the owner unsure any second tab was even open. Branch `claude/library-popup-issue-4oh86u`. Minted B818 via `npm run next-id`; RENUMBERED тЖТ **B819** on merge-in of `origin/main`, which took B816тАУB818 + V306/V307 for the scheduler cadence work. тЖТ V308.)*
`[x]` **FIXED this session тАФ root-caused, fixed at the pure-protocol level, and PROVEN with a standalone repro (bug reproduced true, fix drives it false) + a new regression unit test; full suite green (3755), `eslint` 0 errors, build green, lazy chunks intact.**
- **AUDIT-FIRST root cause тАФ a regression from B669's keep-alive interacting with B313's presence banner.** The Shell keeps every VISITED workspace mounted-but-hidden for instant switching (B669, `Shell.jsx:145`), so a SINGLE tab can have several `AppHeader`s alive at once (e.g. the Library header + a kept-alive Review header on the same project). Each header runs its own `useMultiTab` тЖТ `createMultiTabPresence` (B313), and each got a **fresh random `tabId` per instance** (`multiTab.js`). Because `BroadcastChannel` delivers messages between instances in the **same document** (not only across real tabs), those same-tab headers announced the same project id and saw each other as a *different* tab тЖТ `summarizePresence` set `conflictRisk:true` тЖТ the banner fired with only one real tab open. Compounding it, the banner's "the others are **read-only** until you take over editing there" text describes a lockout the **Library doesn't have** (per-file/per-row ops, no single-active-editor lock), so it was doubly wrong there.
- **The fix (two parts, both minimal):**
  1. *`src/shared/presence/multiTab.js` тАФ ONE presence identity per browsing context.* Added a module-scoped `documentTabId` (lazy `getDocumentTabId()`); `createMultiTabPresence` now uses `opts.tabId || getDocumentTabId()`. A module singleton is per-realm = per-tab: every instance in one tab shares the id (the existing line-71 self-echo guard then makes them ignore each other), while a genuinely separate tab is a fresh realm with its own id тАФ so the real cross-tab warning still fires. Tests pass an explicit `opts.tabId` to simulate distinct tabs inside one realm.
  2. *`src/workspaces/library/Library.jsx` тАФ `multiEditOk` on the Library's `AppHeader`.* The Library supports concurrent multi-tab use (no read-only lockout), so the B313 warning is inapplicable and must not show even across two genuine tabs тАФ same contract the Site Planner uses via `multiwriterEnabled()`.
- Verify: live тЖТ **V308** тАФ the banner renders only for **signed-in** accounts (`accountActive`), and the sandbox blocks sign-in, so the signed-in end-to-end (open the Library on a project after visiting Review in the same tab тЖТ NO banner) parks for a live click-through. The banner *logic* is proven in the sandbox (unit test + standalone protocol repro below).
- Origin: owner-reported 2026-07-13 (single-tab false banner on the Library).
- **Named rules:** AUDIT-FIRST (traced the actual delivery mechanism тАФ BroadcastChannel delivers same-document тАФ and reconciled B313's per-instance-id assumption against the post-B669 kept-alive reality); LIVE-VERIFY (signed-in-only render тЖТ V308); MODULE-SCOPE-COMPONENTS n/a. No `MAP.md` change (no file add/remove/rename, no primary-export change).
- **DEDUPE-FIRST:** net-new. **NOT B759** (that is the Site Planner's element-sync realtime toast "you (another window) changed X" in `elementSync.js` over Supabase Realtime тАФ different module, message, transport, and workspace). Thematically the sibling of the B759 "false another-tab warning in one tab" family; this one is the B313 BroadcastChannel presence banner, regressed by B669's keep-alive. Related: B313 (added the banner), B669 (keep-alive), B674 (`multiEditOk`).
- **Verified (sandbox):** `test/multiTab.test.js` +1 regression case ("two instances in the SAME document never mistake each other for a second tab") тАФ and the two existing real-BroadcastChannel round-trip tests updated to pass explicit distinct tabIds (correctly modelling two real tabs). A standalone node repro against the real `createMultiTabPresence`: distinct per-instance ids in one doc тЖТ `conflictRisk=true` (the bug); shared per-document identity тЖТ `conflictRisk=false` (fixed). Full suite **3755** green ┬╖ `eslint` 0 errors ┬╖ `npm run build` green ┬╖ Library + AppHeader remain separate lazy chunks.

### B817 тАФ Float-to-deadline, cost-of-miss, and the cadence view `[Scheduler]` (feature) #scheduler #entitlements #gantt #export  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-13 as "NEW-3"; minted **B817**. тЖТ V307. The decision-value columns + at-risk health SHIPPED this session; the cadence-view Gantt + loud banners split to **B818**.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED the decision-value core this session (Float / Cost columns + health rollup).** Depends on B816. The math is half the product; the decision value is knowing **what one day of slip actually costs**. In an entitlement schedule a day is routinely a month, and nothing in the current grid says so.
- Verify: live тАФ column math + health rollup unit-testable; the Gantt ticks/flags + the two banner resolutions are **V307**, run via Cowork on live planyr.io.
- Origin: filed 2026-07-13 from chat ("NEW-3").
- **Two grid columns** (Columns chooser `GridColumnsChooser` `:8405`, default on when any task in the project is bound; blank on unbound rows): **"Float to deadline"** тАФ working days from today/packet-ready to the agenda deadline тАФ and **"Cost if missed"** тАФ calendar days from the current meeting to the next eligible one. Derived, non-editable, like B583 formula columns (`e:false`); an existing `col.t==="cost"` family already lives in `COLS` (`:2327`).
- **Gantt:** bound milestones render with the glyph. When a bound row is selected, the body's eligible meeting dates draw as **faint vertical ticks** across the timeline and the agenda deadline draws as a **flag connected to the meeting diamond by a hairline** тАФ you see the cadence and how far the next one is. Route any connector through the existing `depAnchors`/`glyphEdges` path (`:9152`/`:9270`/`:11080`) тАФ do NOT add a second connector renderer. (AUDIT-FIRST: `depElbow`/`depElbowD` in the brief were removed with the elbow router; the current path is `depAnchors`+`glyphEdges`.)
- **Deadline badge** on the driving predecessor's bar ("file by 8/18/26") тАФ the upstream task that actually has to hit the date carries the warning, not just the hearing.
- **Row states, all loud:** deadline passed + unpinned тЖТ auto-rolled (B816) + toast + a "rolled from 8/11" annotation ┬╖ deadline passed + pinned тЖТ infeasible, red row + banner naming the violation, two one-click resolutions (roll / unpin), reusing **B622**'s conflict-surfacing banner ┬╖ meeting date in the past + task not complete тЖТ offer "roll to next meeting" (this is the live state of First Reading of Annexation Ordinance on the board right now).
- **Wire float into `computeDisplayHealth`** (`:1976`) so a bound task at тЙд2 working days of float reads at-risk on the dashboard **before** it slips, not after.
- **Shipped + unit-tested (11 tests):** pure `meetingFloatBD(task, today)` (working days to the agenda deadline) + `meetingCostDays(task, body)` (calendar days to the next eligible meeting), mirrored VERBATIM into `scheduler-engine.mjs` with anti-drift guards. Two derived grid columns тАФ **Float** and **Cost/miss** (`e:false`, `t:"meeting"`, blank on unbound rows) тАФ that **default ON in `readGridCfg` once any task in the project is bound**. Float wired into **`computeDisplayHealth`** (src + mirror): a bound task reads **red** when infeasible and **at-risk yellow** at тЙд2 working days of float, before it slips тАФ proven by 5 health-rollup tests with a deterministic `setNOW`. Full suite green, build green, MAP regenerated, eslint 0, scheduler JSX validated via esbuild.
- **Split to B818 (the visual half, live-only):** the cadence-view Gantt (faint eligible-meeting ticks + the agenda-deadline flag on a selected bound row), the deadline badge on the driving predecessor's bar, the three loud row-state banners (auto-rolled annotation ┬╖ infeasible red-row tint + B622 resolution banner ┬╖ past-meeting "roll to next meeting" offer), and the click-open explainer popover. Filed as **B818** so the tested column/health core ships now; those need a signed-in live check anyway.

### B816 тАФ Meeting-bound tasks: snap to cadence, auto-roll on miss, derived agenda deadline `[Scheduler]` (feature) #scheduler #entitlements #gantt #perf #export  *(owner-dropped 2026-07-13 as "NEW-2"; minted **B816**. тЖТ V306. Implemented + shipped same session; the engine is unit-tested in the sandbox (15 tests), the UI is parked for the live click-through.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED this session тАФ engine + data layer + civic mark + bind picker + roll toast.** Depends on B815. **Own PR, nothing else in it** тАФ this touches `cascadeDates`, the highest-blast-radius function in the codebase (B584/B585/B501/B487/B568 all cluster here). A task bound to a meeting body snaps to the body's cadence, derives its agenda deadline, and **auto-rolls a whole cycle** when the deadline is missed.
- Verify: live тАФ engine end-to-end unit-testable via the verbatim mirror + anti-drift guards; the live click-through (bind a task тЖТ slip a predecessor тЖТ watch it jump a cycle тЖТ pin it тЖТ watch it go red) is **V306**, run via Cowork on live planyr.io (the scheduler's CDN React/Babel is egress-blocked in the sandbox).
- Origin: filed 2026-07-13 from chat ("NEW-2").
- **Task fields `_v7 тЖТ _v8`** via a new `normalizeToV8` (idempotent), chained after the existing `normalizeToV7` (`:4562`): `meetingBodyId ┬╖ meetingBound:true ┬╖ pinnedMeetingDate?`. Existing tasks untouched тАФ a no-op stamp, zero date shift by construction. Run the real before/after diff against the live scheduler dataset (Supabase hs-v1, ~667 tasks) exactly as B621 did. (AUDIT-FIRST: today's version is `_v7`, not `_v8` тАФ B816 adds V8.)
- **тШЕ The agenda deadline is NOT a task row.** It is a **derived field** тАФ a pure function of (body, chosenMeetingDate), recomputed every cascade, never persisted as authoritative, never given an id, never entering `tasks[]` or the dependency graph. Rationale from this repo's history: `renumberTasks`/cut-paste/delete/indent-outdent have each corrupted the task array (B568/B584/B501/B487), so a system-owned row inside a user-owned list reopens all of it; and a real FS link deadlineтЖТmeeting closes a cycle against the meetingтЖТdeadline derivation (`validatePredEdit` rejects it). Precedent: **B583** formula columns (`e:false`, derived, no feedback loop) тАФ except computed *inside* the cascade, because unlike a formula column it participates in date selection.
- **Cascade rule** (in `cascadeDates` `:1861`, after the normal predecessor-derived early start, before `calcEnd`): predecessors produce a packet-ready date; chosen meeting = earliest `m` where **`agendaDeadline(m) >= packetReady`** тАФ NOT `m >= packetReady` (the core of the feature and the obvious wrong implementation; `m >= packetReady` silently puts items on agendas they can't be filed for). `start = end = m`; duration forced to 0d; agenda deadline computed + stored as a derived field for renderers.
- **Tie-break тАФ `sameDayFilingAllowed`, default false:** when the driving predecessor is itself a meeting (first reading тЖТ second reading), eligibility is **`agendaDeadline(m) > drivingMeetingDate`, strictly**. Council meets Tuesday evening; the next agenda closed at noon that same Tuesday тАФ a `>=` produces a schedule that cannot physically happen (at a 10-business-day lead on a 2-week cadence the two readings can never be consecutive and the schedule quietly loses a month). `minMeetingsAfter:{taskId,n}` for two-reading ordinances / "must be a subsequent meeting."
- **тШЕ The mark (ships in THIS item тАФ B816 can't land without it).** A bound row breaks three rules other rows follow (date can't be freely typed ┬╖ duration forced to 0 ┬╖ slips in cycles not days) тАФ a row that behaves differently with no visible reason is a silent-behavior defect. **Glyph:** a bank/civic mark (`ti-building-bank` from the loaded `ti` webfont, or a hand-rolled SVG to match) in the Start-cell glyph slot beside the padlock (`:8895тАУ8924`), distinct from the amber padlock (`pinnedStart`/`pinnedEnd`, **B621/B622** тАФ in-code labels `B615`/`B616`): padlock = a person fixed this date; civic mark = a meeting calendar fixes it. They co-occur on a pinned bound task (ЁЯПЫ 8/11/26 ЁЯФТ) тАФ exactly the state that goes infeasible. **Three states, salience tracking severity:** `--text-secondary` (healthy float) ┬╖ `--text-warning` (тЙд2 working days float) ┬╖ `--text-danger` (infeasible тАФ pinned + agenda closed); solid fills; the row tints `--bg-danger` **only** in the infeasible state. **Clicking the glyph explains the row** тАФ body name, cadence, agenda rule, `verifiedOn` stamp, the plain-English reason the date is what it is, and the resolutions (roll to next meeting / unpin / change body). No DevTools, no dialog.
- **Every roll is announced** тАФ reuse **B624**'s toast verbatim: "First reading moved to 8/25/26 тАФ the 8/11 agenda closed 8/4." A bound date that moves without the user seeing why is a defect, not a convenience.
- **Interaction matrix тАФ each case its own test in `test/schedulerEngine.test.js`.** `cascadeDates` already branches on no-predecessors / pinnedStart / pinnedEnd / dep type (FS-SS-FF-SF via the `switch` inside `constrainedStartFrom` `:1740` тАФ AUDIT-FIRST: `DEP_DIRS` was removed with the elbow router, so hook the new case there, not a named map) / lags / unit-aware duration (`resolveDuration`) / blank-unscheduled. "Meeting-bound" is a fifth orthogonal branch, and this matrix is where the bugs will come from:
  - **bound + pinnedStart** тЖТ pin wins, do not roll тЖТ infeasible flag + red glyph.
  - **bound + pinnedEnd** тЖТ nonsense (start==end==meeting date) тАФ reject on entry.
  - **bound + blank/unscheduled predecessor** тЖТ stays blank (B386's first-class unscheduled state) тАФ must NOT snap to next Tuesday from today.
  - **bound + SS/FF/SF link** тЖТ packet-ready = the normal early start (via `constrainedStartFrom`); snap from there.
  - **bound as a summary/parent** тЖТ disallow (parents come from `rollupParentDates`) тАФ guard in `validatePredEdit`.
  - **bound + typed duration** тЖТ force 0d with a visible inline error, never a silent zero.
- **Also touches:** `updateTask` (`:5157`) ┬╖ `previewProject` (`:3728`, must mirror `updateTask` exactly тАФ B585-S1 was a preview that lied about a pinned task) ┬╖ `mkt` (`:2071`, new-task factory defaults) ┬╖ `applyUpdate` (`:7875`, typing a date into a bound task snaps to the nearest eligible meeting + toast, mirroring B624's weekend roll-forward) ┬╖ `validatePredEdit` (`:1705`).
- **Perf (interacts with B256, Open тАФ the live board is already at 667, past its ~500 threshold):** precompute each body's meeting dates once per cascade run (`meetingDatesInRange(body, projectStart, projectEnd+horizon)`) and binary-search тАФ do NOT generate recurrence dates inside the per-task loop. Strongly consider landing B256's idтЖТindex + parentтЖТchildren[] maps first (makes this cheaper, overdue on its own merits).
- **Both Gantt renderers, or neither.** `GanttView.depLines` (screen, `:9296`) and `buildGanttSVG` (PDF/Print, `:10866`) are separate implementations that have drifted (B386/B395/B584 #11) тАФ either put the glyph + markers in both, or have the export render bound milestones as plain milestones тАФ **state which in the PR** (PDF-PARITY).
- **Shipped:** `cascadeDates(tasks, bodies)` + `applyMeetingBinding` (the snap rule `agendaDeadline(m) >= packetReady`, the strict two-reading tie-break, `minMeetingsAfter`), mirrored VERBATIM into `scheduler-engine.mjs` with **15 unit tests + 3 anti-drift guards** covering the whole matrix (bound+pinnedStartтЖТinfeasible, bound+blank predтЖТblank, bound+SS/FF/SF, bound-as-parent disallowed, typed-durationтЖТ0, the тШЕ two-readings-lose-a-month case). Bodies reach the cascade via a global `MEETING_BODY_INDEX` (like `HOLIDAY_SET`; ids are globally unique so no cross-project bleed; `duplicateProject` RE-IDs copied bodies). `normalizeToV8` is a no-op version stamp that refreshes the index on load. UI: the hand-rolled civic-bank glyph in the Start cell (3 severity states + a plain-English hover explainer), a hidden **Meeting** grid column with a native-select bind picker (`updateTask` re-cascades on the meeting fields; `previewProject` mirrors it), and the B624-voice roll toast when a bound task's meeting moves. Full suite green, `npm run build` green, `MAP.md` regenerated, `eslint` 0 errors, scheduler JSX validated via esbuild.
- **Deferred to follow-ups (noted, not silent):** the explainer is a rich **hover** tooltip (a click-open popover is a small NEW-3-era polish); the `--bg-danger` full-row tint is not yet wired (the red glyph carries the infeasible state); direct-typing a date into a bound row currently pins via the normal path (the snap-to-nearest-meeting-on-type is a refinement). **Both Gantts:** bound tasks are duration-0 **milestones**, so they already render as diamonds in BOTH `GanttView` and `buildGanttSVG` (the export shows the plain milestone тАФ the stated PDF-PARITY fallback; the civic glyph lives in the grid). The live before/after diff against the real ~667-task board + the click-through are **V306**.

### B796 тАФ Rehydrated drainage check must re-derive authority, not trust the stored verdict `[Site Planner / GIS ┬╖ yield]` (bug) #site-planner #gis #yield #persistence  *(filed 2026-07-12 from a Cowork investigation brief as "NEW-1", minted B788; RENUMBERED B788тЖТ**B796** on merge-in of `origin/main` тАФ the concurrent data-deletion-safety session (PR #602) took B784тАУB793; code/tests/commits keep the provisional **B788** label. ### B792 тАФ Review delete-safety: same-name re-upload cross-wires two reviews; delete permanently destroys the markup layer; a network blip renders an empty Library `[Doc Review / Library]` (bug) #doc-review #library #persistence #drive #files  *(found by the 2026-07-12 data-deletion-safety audit as "NEW-F1/F3/F5/F7"; lineage: NEW-4/B579/B757 delete honesty, B54 read-failure discipline. Branch `claude/data-deletion-safety-audit-bw5xg9`; тЖТ V292. RENUMBERED twice on merge-ins of `origin/main` (concurrent sessions took B783, then B784тАУB790/V285тАУV290); the code/commits keep the provisional NEW-F# labels.)*
`[x]` **IMPLEMENTED тАФ four legs, one path:** **(F1)** `buildDriveKey` embeds `srcId` in the key's LAST segment (`project-<pid>/<discipline>/<srcId>__<name>`) so two uploads of the same-named file can never share a key (the old name-only key REBOUND the `drive_files` mapping to the newest Drive file тАФ the older review's backdrop silently swapped, and deleting either review deleted the one mapped file under the other). Legacy keys resolve unchanged (stored on the source record; the server's flat-folder derivation drops the last segment, so folders are byte-identical). Purge-path byte deletes are gated by a **shared-key guard** (jsonb containment over other rows; fail-safe: unconfirmed тЖТ keep bytes + notice). **(F3)** `deleteReview` = SOFT delete (`deleted_at`, migration `doc_reviews_soft_delete.sql` тАФ **applied to production via MCP this session**); Library gains **Recently deleted** (Restore / two-click Delete-forever), worded confirms, a ~10s undo toast; `ReviewsBar`'s `window.confirm` removed (owner rule); lazy 30-day purge; pre-migration DBs degrade to the old hard delete. B757 `.select("id")` + B579 ordering preserved; boot-resume can't reopen a deleted review (`loadReview` hides deleted rows; the local draft clears on soft delete тАФ the cloud row keeps full data for restore). **(F5)** `fetchReviews`/`fetchFileFacts`/`fetchProjects` return `{ok, rows}` (the pinStore pattern); FileBrowser keeps the prior list on a failed refresh + a loud Retry notice тАФ never a fake-empty Library (the panic that walks a user into F1's re-upload). **(F7)** purge also removes the `file_facts` row (full TOMBSTONE-DELETES cascade set). **Post-review hardening (same session тАФ 5-lens adversarial review, 25 raw findings triaged, the real ones fixed):** the `fetchReviews` fallback tiers are now GATED on a genuinely-missing `deleted_at` column (a transient error on a migrated DB is an honest `ok:false`, never a filterless re-query that would resurface Recently-deleted rows); `listDeletedReviews` returns null on a failed read (the bin keeps its last list, mirrors NEW-F5); the automated 30-day purge surfaces stranded-bytes cleanup failures; the undo toast fires only on a delete that really landed (0-row no-op тЖТ loud notice, B757 honesty); the bin view can't strand you without an exit toggle; ReviewsBar's row keyboard handler no longer hijacks Enter from the inline confirm, and an armed confirm disarms on menu close. **Accepted semantics (documented in the migration file):** on a TEAM-shared review, any member can bin/restore (rides the member-wide UPDATE policy тАФ same editors who can already rewrite content; recoverable by design), while permanent purge keeps the stricter owner/team-admin DELETE policy.
